{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:35:57","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:35:57","title":"How to Create Irresistible Facebook Landing Pages (Examples)","link":"http://unbounce.com/?p=15015","description":"\n<p>Imagine a potential customer is sitting in their car, waiting to pick up their kids from school. They&#8217;ve got 15 minutes to kill, so they pick up their phone and (because they&#8217;re 46 and don&#8217;t know about TikTok yet) scroll through Facebook.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Between checking out their best friend&#8217;s pictures from a tropical vacation and trying to untangle their Aunt Ida&#8217;s&#8230; uh, &#8220;unorthodox&#8221; political insights, they see your Facebook advertisement for gorgeous, handmade leather bags.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Your ads reach people like this because of tracking, pixels, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://unbounce.com/social-media/facebook-lookalike-audiences/\" target=\"_blank\">lookalike audiences</a>, and all the other technical magic that powers Facebook&#8217;s advertising platform. Facebook can see that this potential customer is in the market for a new leather bag (they were just searching for one last night!) and, based on the demographic targeting you&#8217;ve applied, shows them your ad.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>There are only five minutes left until the school bell rights and children flood out the doors into the car, demanding snacks, Fortnite V-Bucks, and meaningful action to address global climate change. So, your prospect clicks your ad with the intent to buy.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Only&#8230; <strong>your Facebook ad doesn&#8217;t send them where they expected</strong>. Instead, it takes them to the homepage of your store. The beautiful leather bag you were advertising is nowhere in sight. Now the kids are in the car, the phone is back in the console, and the sale is lost. Where&#8217;d you go wrong?</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In this article, we&#8217;re going to discuss how <strong>dedicated Facebook landing pages help you capture more of these near-miss conversions</strong>. Along the way, we&#8217;ll highlight ways you can optimize your pages to make &#8217;em more impactful and share some examples of digital brands who&#8217;re doing it right.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"blog-cta-image-section\" data-ga=\"\"><a href=\"https://unbounce.com/solutions/use-case/social-ads/\" target=\"_blank\" data-campaign=\"\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/blog-visual-cta-generic-social-lightgrey.jpg\" alt=\"Landing Pages with Social Media\" width=\"2260\" height=\"1216\" /></a></div>\n\n\n<h2><strong>What Is a Facebook Landing Page?</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>A Facebook landing page is a dedicated page designed to convert visitors from a specific <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://unbounce.com/solutions/use-case/ppc/\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>pay-per-click (PPC)</strong></a> Facebook ad</strong>. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>These landing pages are different from other pages (like product pages on your website) because they&#8217;re tailor-made to complement your Facebook ad. They continue the story—the hook, the design, the call to action that was introduced to the reader as they scrolled through their Facebook newsfeed.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Years ago, Facebook offered landing pages within their own platform. These allowed businesses to gate their content for Facebook likes (earning them the nickname &#8220;like gate&#8221;), but they haven&#8217;t been available since 2014.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In this post, when we talk about Facebook landing pages, we&#8217;re talking about the first page someone sees after they click on a Facebook ad—not to be confused with the on-platform landing pages Facebook used to offer.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Why Do I Need Landing Pages for My Facebook Ads?</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Everyone&#8217;s Facebook newsfeed is unique. The content and pages you like, the friends you&#8217;re connected to, the groups you&#8217;re joined—these things all influence the way your newsfeed populates. Because prospects&#8217; newsfeeds are personalized and the ads they see are highly targeted, your Facebook landing page needs to be tightly aligned with your ad if it&#8217;s going to be successful.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Here are some other reasons that having dedicated landing pages for each Facebook ad is good practice:</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Potential customers need more information</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Scrollers, readers, and browsers on Facebook need extra nurturing to go from ad click to purchase. These potential customers are in the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brand_awareness\">brand awareness phase</a>. To convert on your page, they&#8217;ll wanna see specific information related to whatever got them to click on the ad in the first place. A focused Facebook landing page—with concise info and a consistent message—is the best way to turn them into customers.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Mobile users are distracted users</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>People don&#8217;t log into Facebook for in-depth reading and focused learning. They&#8217;re filling time, or just picking up their phone for a quick check-in. And because <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://sproutsocial.com/insights/facebook-stats-for-marketers/\" target=\"_blank\">94% of Facebook ad revenue is from a mobile device</a>, you should assume everyone who sees your ad only has five minutes or less to make a purchase. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>That&#8217;s why you need to make it as easy as possible to go from Facebook ad to landing page call to action. Every navigation obstacle or confusing message risks losing your prospect&#8217;s attention and having them move on to something else.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Homepages are slow and overwhelming</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Homepages are great for solution-aware prospects looking for specific information, but they can be overwhelming for visitors from social media. (Just think of all the distractions: nav bars, calls to action, lists of products and features.) A MECLABS study found that <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.smallbizdaily.com/5-common-problems-b2b-lead-generation-fix-them/#:~:text=According%20to%20MECLABS%2044%25%20of,cost%20you%20that%20lead%2C%20forever.\" target=\"_blank\">44% of clicks generated by B2B companies send readers to a homepage</a> and not a dedicated landing page. That&#8217;s a lot of businesses that aren&#8217;t optimizing for conversions. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>An average visitor <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.marketingdive.com/news/google-53-of-mobile-users-abandon-sites-that-take-over-3-seconds-to-load/426070/#:~:text=Dive%20Brief%3A,seconds%20on%20a%204G%20connection.\" target=\"_blank\">won&#8217;t wait more than three seconds for a page to load</a>.  Most websites are heavy with images, scripts, and other elements that make them slower than an optimized landing page. When you send your Facebook ad traffic to your homepage, you&#8217;re probably losing more customers than you realize. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>How Do I Create a High-Converting Facebook Landing Page</strong>?</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>We&#8217;ve got a quick-reference list of Facebook <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-articles/landing-page-best-practices/\" target=\"_blank\">landing page best practices</a> below, but there are two things you really wanna keep in mind as you start building your page:</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Know your audience</strong>. It&#8217;s no secret that Facebook has amazing targeting capabilities, but you won&#8217;t be able to take advantage of them if you don&#8217;t know anything about your ideal prospects. Before you shell out the cash for Facebook ads, make sure that you know your audience well. Spend time investigating how potential customers search for your solution, what words they use when describing products or services similar to yours, and what features or benefits interest them most. </p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Keep it consistent</strong>. When writing for a Facebook landing page, remember to keep the messaging consistent between your ad and your landing page. Marketers might think that repeating copy is repetitive, but it can help reinforce your message to prospects and reassure them they&#8217;re in the right place after they click. Same with calls to action: if someone clicks an ad about earning a doctoral degree, that&#8217;d better be the main focus of your landing page. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2><em>5 Facebook Landing Page Must-Haves</em></h2>\n\n\n\n<ol><li><strong>Clear unique selling proposition (USP)</strong>. Visitors should immediately be able to tell what makes your product or service a fit for their needs. Don&#8217;t bury the most important details lower on your page—show &#8217;em above the fold.</li><li><strong>Strong, descriptive headlines</strong>. Your headline should make the reader want to know more or see more. The headline on both the Facebook ad and landing page should convey the same offer.</li><li><strong>Consistent design elements</strong>. The goal here is to continue the story you started on Facebook, and that includes visuals. If the images on your Facebook ad are neutral colors with images of smiling kids, then your Facebook landing page should also have neutral colors with images of smiling kids.</li><li><strong>High-quality images or videos</strong>. This seems like a gimme, but you&#8217;d be surprised how many Facebook landing pages use low-res visuals that scare off prospects right after they&#8217;ve clicked an ad. Make sure to use images or <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-articles/the-benefits-of-using-video-on-landing-pages/\">videos on your landing page</a> that shows your offer in the best light.</li><li><strong>A singular, compelling call to action</strong>. You can repeat your call to action throughout the page, but you should only ask visitors to do one specific thing. Plus, your copy should tell them exactly what happens when they do that thing: for example, &#8220;get the ebook&#8221; rather than &#8220;submit&#8221; on a form.</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Examples of Facebook Landing Pages Done Right</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Of course, we&#8217;d never give you all this information without providing some concrete examples. Here&#8217;s a breakdown of Facebook landing pages from Unbounce customers who really know what they&#8217;re doing. </p>\n\n\n\n<hr class=\"wp-block-separator\"/>\n\n\n\n<h2>Quarters: Target Your Ads with Demographic Information</h2>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://quarters.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Quarters</a> is an all-inclusive community living space in multiple locations around the world. They advertise their service on Facebook by highlighting their transparent pricing, contract flexibility, and included amenities.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This Facebook ad that Quarters is running has five variants. Each features copy and imagery designed to target people looking for housing in a particular city or neighborhood—say, Manhattan—allowing Facebook to surface relevant ads depending on audience location.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_Quarters.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Quarters_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Facebook Landing Page Examples - Quarters\" class=\"wp-image-97855\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://quarters.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Quarters</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>When someone clicks through to the landing page, Quarters encourages them to &#8220;Check Availability,&#8221; repeating the call to action throughout the page to keep it top-of-mind. This does a great job of guiding visitors to take the next step in the purchase journey.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Choosing a place to live can be a substantial expense (especially in the Big Apple), and Quarters anticipates their prospects will have plenty of questions. The landing page includes tons of useful information, including 360-degree tours of available rooms, details on the neighborhoods (with images and maps), and quick-reference lists of amenities and pricing.</p>\n\n\n\n<hr class=\"wp-block-separator\"/>\n\n\n\n<h2>TapSnap + Samuraw: Give Visitors Everything They Need to Convert</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Here are a couple of landing pages that show it&#8217;s often more important to be clear than clever.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.tapsnap.net/\" target=\"_blank\">TapSnap</a> is a photo booth rental company and their Facebook landing page makes that obvious. Above the fold, their message is super straightforward: they&#8217;re selling photo booths, they&#8217;ll deliver them to you, here&#8217;s how to get in touch. <em>Boom</em>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Side note: Check out the arrow at the bottom of the fold that directs your eye to more information. Without it, the page might&#8217;ve created a <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://cxl.com/blog/false-bottom/\" target=\"_blank\">false bottom</a> effect, leading people to believe that they were at the bottom of the page when there&#8217;s actually more to read. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_Tapsnap.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Tapsnap_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Facebook Landing Page Examples - TapSnap\" class=\"wp-image-97859\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://www.tapsnap.net/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">TapSnap</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Further down, TapSnap provides a concise, skimmable list of features that help prospects quickly understand what they can expect from the product. Plus, the brand shows its booths in action with photos from real events (alongside examples of the different kinds of pictures available) to show off the experience they create. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>TapSnap doesn&#8217;t leave anything to the imagination—and neither does <a href=\"https://www.samuraw.ca/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Samuraw</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Samuraw offers a high-quality mineral and probiotic supplement made from natural ingredients, and this Facebook landing page (built by <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.webistry.com/\" target=\"_blank\">Webistry</a>) delivers that message right away in the headline. By including the &#8220;add to cart&#8221; call to action above the fold, Samuraw also gives visitors a clear path to purchase.  </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_Samuraw.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Samuraw_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Facebook Landing Page Examples - Samuraw\" class=\"wp-image-97856\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://www.samuraw.ca/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Samuraw</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>If you&#8217;re already in the market for a real-food multivitamin and probiotic (who isn&#8217;t?), you might choose to purchase right them. But if you&#8217;re curious about ingredients and other nutritional details, Samuraw has done a great job of providing all that information further down the page.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Another neat feature of this Samuraw landing page is the sticky call to action that follows visitors as they scroll the page. This helps keep the offer top of mind and makes it easy for readers to purchase the product when they&#8217;re ready to convert.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"curated-tip\">\n    <div class=\"container inner text-left\">\n        <p><strong>Wanna see how other brands are using Facebook landing pages to grow their businesses?</strong> Check out this post about <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/campaign-strategy/baby-food-brand-brought-in-email-subscribers/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">how a baby food brand used Facebook to create an email list of 14,000+ subscribers</a>, or this one about <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/ppc/how-indochino-uses-unbounce-for-ppc/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">how Indochino drove 50% growth</a> in just one year. </p>\n    </div>\n</div>\n\n\n<h2>Taboola + TurnKey: Use Proof Points to Establish Credibility</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Leveraging proof (like evidence of your supposed benefits or testimonials from happy customers) in your Facebook ad and landing page copy is a powerful way to create trust with your audience.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Take <a href=\"https://www.taboola.com/advertisers\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Taboola</a>, an advertising and sponsored content platform that you&#8217;ve probably seen surfacing content all over the web. In this Facebook ad, Taboola makes sure to highlight their expansive digital network: &#8220;Reach 1.4B users &#8211; and get traffic that converts.&#8221; </p>\n\n\n\n<p>That&#8217;s a huge benefit that&#8217;s sure to get the attention of businesses who wanna get their message in front of loads of prospects.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_Taboola.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Taboola_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Facebook Landing Page Examples - Taboola\" class=\"wp-image-97858\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://www.taboola.com/advertisers\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Taboola</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Taboola continues to build trust on their Facebook landing page. Above the fold, they&#8217;ve included a banner of some of their most recognizable partners and customers: USA Today, IKEA, and Microsoft, to name a few. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Further down, Taboola even includes concrete results that brands have gotten with the platform. It&#8217;s one thing to say you can increase someone&#8217;s conversion rate or audience engagement. It&#8217;s another thing to prove it with hard numbers.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.turnkeyvr.com/\" target=\"_blank\">TurnKey</a> gives us another great example of how to use proof on your Facebook landing page. As a vacation rental platform, the company needs visitors to trust that their properties will be handled with care. They do that by including featured media logos and various awards in a banner above the fold.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_Turnkey.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Turnkey_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Facebook Landing Page Examples - TurnKey\" class=\"wp-image-97860\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://www.turnkeyvr.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">TurnKey</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>But the most compelling proof on this page is a testimonial that TurnKey includes lower down. This customer totally lays out TurnKey&#8217;s unique selling proposition: other rental platforms have left their home in shambles and failed to earn them what they expected, whereas TurnKey puts their mind at ease by protecting the property from damage and generating more revenue. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>You&#8217;ve gotta hire this guy, TurnKey. </p>\n\n\n\n<hr class=\"wp-block-separator\"/>\n\n\n\n<h2>CommuniCloud: Convert More with a Compelling Incentive</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Sure, your offer is great—but to <em>really</em> get people converting, it can help to give &#8217;em a little something extra. For ecommerce companies, maybe it&#8217;s free shipping or a discount. For SaaS brands, it&#8217;s usually a no-commitment free trial.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>That&#8217;s how <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.communicloud.com/\">CommuniCloud</a> is driving registrations on this Facebook landing page. The brand keeps things simple: along with a quick description of their benefits and some social proof, we&#8217;ve got a quick form that asks just for necessary information. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_Communicloud.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Communicloud_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Facebook Landing Page Examples - CommuniCloud\" class=\"wp-image-97860\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://www.communicloud.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Communicloud</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>It&#8217;s important to note that CommuniCloud <em>doesn&#8217;t require a credit card</em> to sign up for their trial. That&#8217;d create some serious friction at this stage, so better to capture contact details and sort out the payment side later.</p>\n\n\n\n<hr class=\"wp-block-separator\"/>\n\n\n\n<h2>Schedulehead + HiredHippo: Show Off the Product In Action</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Some products are&#8230; let&#8217;s say, <em>more photogenic</em> than others. It&#8217;s easier to get people&#8217;s attention with a picture of food or clothing than something like software. Still, showing off your product—whatever it is—can better (and more quickly) communicate what you&#8217;re offering than words alone.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.schedulehead.com/\" target=\"_blank\">Schedulehead</a> is a software platform that helps companies manage their employee scheduling and payroll. On this Facebook landing page, the brand is sure to highlight their user interface right from the beginning—before even getting into the specifics of their functionality. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_Schedulehead.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Schedulehead_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Facebook Landing Page Examples - Schedulehead\" class=\"wp-image-97857\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://www.schedulehead.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Schedulehead</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>This helps visitors understand that Schedulehead isn&#8217;t some overrated spreadsheet. There are at-a-glance graphs and charts, map and calendar integrations, and loads of other features to help track your workforce.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And check out this page from <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://signup.hiredhippo.ai/\" target=\"_blank\">HiredHippo</a>, a job search network that automatically matches professionals with hiring companies. (Love this headline, by the way. Finding job opportunities without updating a dull resume sounds like a dream come true.)</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_HiredHippo.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/HiredHippo_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Facebook Landing Page Examples - HiredHippo\" class=\"wp-image-97857\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://signup.hiredhippo.ai/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">HiredHippo</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>After listing some of the benefits and sharing testimonials from users, HiredHippo is sure to include a snapshot of the platform to show visitors what they can expect. Even just from this image, we can see that the dashboard makes evaluating job opportunities way easier by sharing the key details in a bulleted list. </p>\n\n\n\n<hr class=\"wp-block-separator\"/>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Start Building Your Own Facebook Landing Pages with Unbounce</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Ready to create a landing page for your next Facebook ad campaign? 08:35:57","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:35:57","title":"Sales Pages: High-Converting Tips & 5 Can’t-Miss Examples","link":"https://unbounce.com/?p=97999","description":"\n<p>Sales pages are like the powerlifters of landing pages. Or, if team sports are more your thing, they’re the MVPs.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Where most landing pages provide immense value by setting <em>you</em> up to score a sale—perhaps by generating, vetting, or capturing leads—a sales page makes the touchdown itself. (Am I doing this sports metaphor thing right?)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In other words, sales pages have loftier goals than your average product page or landing page. Rather than aiming for downloads, signups, or click-throughs (all of which play a role in finding and nurturing leads), <strong>the purpose of sales pages is turning ad clicks directly into paying customers</strong>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Suffice it to say, the pressure is <em>on</em>. Your sales pages need to come through with the win, which means you need to know how to create a high-converting sales page for every campaign.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In this article, we’ll tell you what makes a great sales landing page and show you how to create a sales page that actually converts clicks into customers. Plus, we’ll look at what you can learn from some of our favorite real-world sales page examples.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But first, let’s answer some of the most common questions related to sales pages for online stores and services.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Everything You Wanted to Know About Sales Landing Pages</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<h3>What is a sales page, exactly?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>A sales page is a dedicated landing page built to convert ad traffic into customers</strong>. You can think of sales pages as the modern sales letter, but more targeted and data-driven. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>A good sales page is more than just a convenient place to send click-throughs. It’s the best place to send someone who clicks on a targeted ad, whether you’re running <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://unbounce.com/solutions/use-case/social-ads/\" target=\"_blank\">paid ads on Instagram</a> or an <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://unbounce.com/solutions/use-case/email-marketing/\" target=\"_blank\">email marketing campaign</a>. </p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Why do I need a sales landing page?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Compared to online stores, sales pages convert better in terms of volume and revenue. In fact, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://info.monetate.com/rs/092-TQN-434/images/EQ1-2018_First-Impressions.pdf\" target=\"_blank\">landing pages have been shown</a> to convert 2X as many visitors into customers and increase average customer spend 2X. <em>Whoa</em>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>A big reason for this is that online stores have built-in distractions that can pull visitors in multiple directions (things like links to related products, promotions, shipping details, etc.). <strong>You use a sales page when you want to maintain momentum and ensure shoppers only have one thing on their mind: making the purchase</strong>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>What separates a sales page from a typical landing page?\n</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Like every great landing page, a sales page is built around a specific conversion goal. However, when it comes to sales page design, the objective isn’t just any old conversion—it’s getting visitors to actually buy. In order to close the deal, a sales page might be longer than the average landing page, especially for bigger purchases.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>What about product pages vs. sales pages?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>If you already have product pages, do you still need sales landing pages?  Um, <em>heck yes!</em> Unlike product pages, which highlight features in depth, a sales landing page is built specifically to convert. That means visitors see the exact information they need to make a purchasing decision, without the distractions typically found on a product page.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Plus, sales landing pages are more flexible than traditional product pages. They can be tweaked and tested and updated before you could even begin making changes to the rest of your website.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"blog-cta-image-section\" data-ga=\"\"><a href=\"https://unbounce.com/ecommerce-lookbook/\" target=\"_blank\" data-campaign=\"\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/LookBook-Blog-Visual-CTA_2.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"538\" /></a></div>\n\n\n<h2><strong>How Do I Create a Sales Page That Converts?</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>A sales landing page is a tool to drive, well, sales. As such, it must be carefully designed to motivate leads to take action. Whether you’re creating a new sales page or hoping to optimize an existing page, there are a few key notes you need to hit. So, what goes into crafting a high-converting sales landing page?\n</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Your sales page needs to match the ad so visitors instantly recognize that they’re in the right place</strong>. Nothing derails a potential sale faster than a page that has little or nothing to do with whatever was featured in the ad (this is basically the ecommerce version of catfishing).</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This is perhaps the most important (and often underestimated) part of an effective sales page, so here’s a quick example.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s say you’re marketing a subscription service for a range of fancy jams and jellies, but this month you’re using paid ads to promote lavender honey from a local farm. It’s seasonal and supplies are limited, so it’s not something you want to add to your website’s regular catalog.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Whoever clicks on that ad has already told you they&#8217;re interested in the lavender honey (why else would they have clicked?). That means they don’t want to see that you offer ice wine jelly or canning supplies (at least, not right at that moment).</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So, what does your sales page need to do? Show them the honey—and, hopefully, they’ll show you the money. Sweet, right?</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Use persuasive copy. </strong>Your sales page needs to do the job of a salesperson, which means compelling leads to open their wallets. The headline should convey immediate benefits and the body copy should be used to address sales objections, answer potential questions, and compel visitors to click ‘buy.’&#160;</li><li><strong>Show the product in action. </strong>Sometimes, simply showing the product in use is the best way to communicate value. Include visuals of the product in action to get customers excited about their upcoming purchase.</li><li><strong>Build trust with social proof. </strong>Address potential sales objections with real testimonials from existing customers. This helps potential customers see the value your product provides and adds credibility to your claims.</li><li><strong>Provide clear next steps. </strong>You don’t want to pay for ads that lead to a dead end. Maintain momentum by featuring a single, straightforward call-to-action on a prominent, clickable button so the next steps are 100% clear.</li></ul>\n\n\n<div class=\"curated-tip\">\n    <div class=\"container inner text-left\">\n        <p><strong>Ready to build a high-converting sales page of your own?</strong> Check out our library of 100+ ready-to-use <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-templates/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">sales page templates</a> and start selling more today.</p>\n    </div>\n</div>\n\n\n<h2><strong>High-Converting Sales Page Examples Created with Unbounce</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<h2>1. Dinnerly</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Dinnerly_Full.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Dinnerly_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Sales Landing Page Examples - Dinnerly\" class=\"wp-image-98017\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://dinnerly.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Dinnerly</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>From the creators of Marley Spoon, <a href=\"https://dinnerly.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Dinnerly</a> is an alternative meal kit service for the budget-conscious home chef. Their price per meal is roughly half of typical meal kits, but their recipes still pack a full-plate, high-quality punch. They’re able to pull this off by minimizing costs related to packaging and marketing.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For this campaign, Dinnerly advertised on Reddit and sent click-throughs to the sales landing page shown above.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Why does this sales page convert so well?</strong><br>This page is built specifically for leads from a single source: Reddit. From the headline to the CTA (“Claim My Reddit Discount”), everything about this page is tailored to the leads who click through from a Reddit ad campaign. Greeting visitors with “Hi Reddit!” immediately tells them they’re in the right place. As we scroll down, the page continues to match both the source and the brand.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>What can you learn from Dinnerly?</strong><br>What can other marketers learn from this example and apply to their own pages? The big takeaway here is to <strong><em>match the message and design of your sales page to the ad</em></strong>. If you want to run similar campaigns across several sources (say, Reddit, Facebook, and Instagram), you should consider building and customizing variant sales pages for each one.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>2. Ruby</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Ruby_Full.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Ruby_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Sales Landing Page Examples - Ruby\" class=\"wp-image-98018\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://www.ruby.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Ruby</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.ruby.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Ruby</a> provides virtual reception and chat services to a wide range of businesses. On this sales landing page, they’re speaking directly to business owners who need live phone support.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Why is this page so great at selling?</strong><br>If you’re looking for inspiration on how to write a sales page, this is it. Both the headline and supporting copy reinforce benefits in terms relevant to the audience.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>All of the content (including benefits, visuals, and pricing information) is targeted towards businesses that need virtual reception and are concerned about missing customer calls or not being able to handle after-hours conversations.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This landing page also wins because it:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>Frames customer testimonials as “Success Stories” to add clout to standard social proof.&#160;</li><li>Features data from customer surveys to demonstrate proven results.</li><li>Emphasizes their money-back guarantee, which addresses some of the biggest sales objections. (“Is it worth the cost? Will I regret this purchase?”)</li><li>Minimizes external distractions by focusing on the receptionist services (rather than looping in their live chat offering).</li><li>Visually divides sections and uses color-blocking to make it easier to scroll for relevant information.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>What can you learn from Ruby’s sales page example?</strong><br>A good sales page provides answers to everything potential customers need to confidently make an informed purchase. Even if you offer tiered services (like Ruby’s monthly packages of 100, 200, or 500 receptionist minutes), you can leverage a single sales page to drive conversions for all of them. The key is to aim for transparency about pricing and packages, so leads don’t have to click away from your sales page to learn more.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you need to provide extra information that doesn’t fit on the main page, you can use lightbox popups like Ruby does for their monthly plans. This is a clever way to keep visitors on the page without bogging down the main content with excessive details that might not be relevant to each visitor.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>3. Thistle</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Thistle_Full.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Thistle_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Sales Landing Page Examples - Thistle\" class=\"wp-image-98020\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://www.thistle.co/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Thistle</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://www.thistle.co/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Thistle</a> is a ready-to-eat meal subscription service that specializes in nutritious, plant-based dishes made from local ingredients.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Why does this sales page get results?</strong><br>One of the simplest things that makes a sales page effective is focusing on the benefits instead of features. The headline highlights what the visitor cares about most (meals that are “so deliciously easy”) and the rest of the copy uses language that says Thistle truly <em>gets</em> what their audience wants.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Even though text only takes up a third of the space above the fold (allowing that bright, veggie-filled salad to do much of the talking), all of these heavy hitters are visible <em>before</em> we scroll down: &#8220;no more groceries,&#8221; &#8220;fill your fridge,&#8221; &#8220;super healthy,&#8221; &#8220;gourmet meals,&#8221; &#8220;less cost.&#8221;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>How can you apply these lessons to your own sales pages?</strong><br>In a highly competitive space, you need something that makes you stand out. Your sales page should balance speaking to your audience’s needs (which your competitors are likely also doing) and emphasizing your unique selling point (which is specific only to your brand). For Thistle, this means highlighting the traditional convenience and benefits of a meal delivery service, but also leaning into the health benefits that set them apart.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"curated-tip\">\n    <div class=\"container inner text-left\">\n        <p><strong>Craving more inspiration for your sales page design?</strong> Take a look at how <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/ppc/how-indochino-uses-unbounce-for-ppc/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Indochino</a> and <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-examples/how-ecommerce-company-packlane-delivers-on-brand-targeted-campaigns-with-custom-landing-pages/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Packlane</a> use Unbounce sales pages to fuel their digital marketing strategy and online sales.</p>\n    </div>\n</div>\n\n\n<h2>4. Solo Stove</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/SoloStove_Full.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/SoloStove_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Sales Landing Page Examples - Solo Stove\" class=\"wp-image-98019\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://www.solostove.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Solo Stove</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>This sales page is part of a retargeting campaign for customers who’ve already purchased the <a href=\"https://www.solostove.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Solo Stove</a> and potentially other accessories.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>What makes this sales page a winner?</strong><br>There are a few reasons why this sales page is so effective. Not only does it appeal to the community that’s built up around their brand, but it also uses visuals that show the product in action.&#160;&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Plus, by introducing the shield as their “most-requested accessory,” Solo Stove implies that their customers already want this. This serves two purposes.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>First, for anyone who may have actually requested the shield, this page offers pure validation. If you even <em>thought</em> about wanting a shield for your Solo Stove and saw this campaign, you’re pretty much guaranteed to buy into it right away. As for the rest of Solo Stove’s customers retargeted by this campaign, the idea that it’s highly requested primes them to convert by building social proof right into the offer.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This page also makes use of a clever CTA (“Claim your Shield” above the “Shop Now” button) that suggests Solo Stove customers are entitled to the shield after eagerly awaiting its release.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>What can you learn from Solo Stove?</strong><br>When you offer multiple products, using sales pages creates space to focus on just one item at a time. That said, you can play around with the formula to best serve your campaign. Unlike most of the other sales pages we’re discussing today, this one breaks the mold a little by linking out to three purchase pages instead of driving all traffic to one.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Solo Stove included three separate “Shop Now” buttons to match the three sizes offered. However, splitting up traffic works here because anyone who clicks on this ad is already a Solo Stove customer. That means they already own a fire pit in one of these sizes—and since the shields are named to match each size, there’s no question of which button each customer should click.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>5. The Coffee Network</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CoffeeNetwork_Full.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CoffeeNetwork_Thumb.png\" alt=\"Sales Landing Page Examples - The Coffee Network\" class=\"wp-image-98016\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">Image courtesy of <a href=\"https://thecoffeenetwork.com.au/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">The Coffee Network</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://thecoffeenetwork.com.au/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">The Coffee Network</a> is an Australia-based coffee marketplace for bean lovers with an appetite for trying new blends.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>What makes this sales page stand out?</strong><br>Presumably, the audience here is already interested in coffee and likely searching online for the best coffee or, more specifically, the best coffee in Australia. That said, this sale page still has to <em>sell</em>—especially because the target audience is likely unfamiliar with the Coffee Network.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>With a focus on benefits and customization (roasting method, strength, and flavor), the copy describes the coffee finder tool both clearly and succinctly. The three steps under “How It Works” are easy to understand at a glance. The call to action repeatedly urges coffee lovers to “try now” and the heading and body copy reiterate how simple it is to use.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Aside from a single link in the footer that leads to their homepage (which prevents leads from bouncing if they aren’t quite ready to buy), this sales page is free of external links and distractions. Including minimal links, offers, and buttons helps keep leads on the page until they’re ready to “Try Now” or grab more information from the website.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>What can you learn from this sales page example?</strong><br>Shorter landing pages work best for products that are simple, smaller purchases (i.e., products that don’t require as much deliberation or persuasion). For most of us, buying coffee isn’t all that complicated. So, in this example, a short and simple sales page hits the spot. The ideal length of any sales page depends on what you’re selling. However, when it comes to deciding <em>what</em> to include on your sales page, quality content always trumps quantity.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"curated-tip\">\n    <div class=\"container inner text-left\">\n        <p><strong>Need even more sales page samples in your life?</strong> Check out our list of <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/conversion-rate-optimization/ecommerce-landing-page-examples-sales/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">27 landing page examples that drive online sales</a>.</p>\n    </div>\n</div>\n\n\n<h2><strong>Put the Power of Sales Pages to Work for Your Business</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>It’s easy to assume that whoever clicks on your ad is interested in your business—in which case, it would make sense to take them to your online store or product page to learn more about your offerings. But, as you know, that’s <em>not</em> why shoppers click ads for individual products or services.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>They don’t care about the rest of your product line (at least, not at that moment). They just want to know more about what you promised them in the ad. So, sending ad traffic straight to your website or product page likely isn’t going to lead to a sale.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Even if you have products or services that practically sell themselves, creating a campaign-specific sales page prevents leads from getting lost on your website instead of following through with the purchase.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you want to grow your online sales without scaling your sales team (and costs), you need dedicated sales pages built to drive revenue. Discover how sales landing pages can take your conversions to the next level.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"blog-cta-image-section\" data-ga=\"\"><a href=\"https://unbounce.com/solutions/industry/ecommerce/\" Bauer","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/LookBook-Blog-Visual-CTA_2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn83@2020_5/2020/08/25/00-35-57-938_e738655a849bb29a.webp","https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Dinnerly_Thumb.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn36@2020_2/2020/08/25/00-36-01-352_9c910fad0e7664c9.webp","https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Ruby_Thumb.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn84@2020_2/2020/08/25/00-36-01-850_c85e1d516e03450b.webp","https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Thistle_Thumb.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn24@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-36-01-876_022f19d33e0f3e81.webp","https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/SoloStove_Thumb.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn27@2020_6/2020/08/25/00-36-01-482_5a9a791e93c8d80c.webp","https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CoffeeNetwork_Thumb.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn19@2020_3/2020/08/25/00-36-04-535_f82cb3419538db38.webp","https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/blog-visual-cta-generic-ecomm-green.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn99@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-36-02-275_e61a04884ede4229.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598315757677},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:35:57","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:35:57","title":"(Guide) How to Choose & Customize a Landing Page Template","link":"https://unbounce.com/?p=98117","description":"\n<p>Let’s say you’re the owner of a boutique soap store and you’re <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/campaign-strategy/how-to-start-online-business-quickly/\">taking your business online</a>. (Hey, in 2020, you wouldn’t be the only one.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You’ve already got a simple website, but you wanna run promotions to really lather up some business. So, <strong>you get to work on your marketing campaign</strong>. You come up with an irresistible offer. You spend your lunch hours <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/campaign-strategy/how-to-build-an-email-list/\">building an email list</a> of existing and potential customers. You stay up late <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/ppc/google-ads-basics/\">learning the basics of Google Ads</a>. Then you start planning the landing page where you’ll send your campaign traffic.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>With all the work you’ve already put in, you’re delighted to know you can save some time by starting with a <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-templates/\">landing page template</a>. But when you go to choose one in your favorite builder (<em>ahem</em>), you don’t see any that look right for your business. There’s a template that seems like it’s meant for realtors, maybe. Another that’d be good for bakeries. But nothing for soap sellers like you. <strong>You’re stuck</strong>.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-98215\" srcset=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template.png 2880w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-150x80.png 150w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-471x250.png 471w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-80x43.png 80w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-768x408.png 768w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-1536x816.png 1536w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-2048x1088.png 2048w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-1000x531.png 1000w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-650x345.png 650w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-300x159.png 300w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Choose_Template-160x85.png 160w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2880px) 100vw, 2880px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<div><p style=\"text-align:center; font-size:80%;\">&#8220;Dangit, Unbounce. Where&#8217;re the soap landing pages?&#8221; — You, probably.</p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Not so fast, sudsy—you’re looking at this the wrong way. The idea here isn’t to find a landing page template that matches your business <em>exactly</em>. First and foremost, you want to <strong>choose a template that supports your campaign conversion goal</strong>. Everything else—your industry, your product or service, your branding—comes second.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In this post, we’ll show you how to pick out the perfect template for your next marketing campaign. Then, we’ll show you <strong>how you can transform it into a custom-branded, high-converting masterpiece</strong>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>How to Choose a Template That Supports Your Conversion Goal</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<h3>What’s a conversion goal, exactly?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Your conversion goal is the action you want visitors to take as a result of your marketing campaign</strong>. Maybe you want somebody to buy a product, like fancy soap. Or maybe you want them to sign up for a webinar about… I dunno, making fancy soap?</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The point is that <strong>some landing page templates are better-suited to specific conversion goals than others</strong>. If you just want someone to buy a product, your landing page’s call to action is pretty straightforward. On the other hand, if you’re registering people for a webinar, you’re gonna need their name and email address (at least). That’ll mean a more complex call to action.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Which template is best for your conversion goal? </h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Broadly, landing page templates fall into one of two categories: <strong>click-through pages </strong>and <strong>lead generation pages</strong>. They’ve each got a distinct type of call to action meant to support a certain conversion goal.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-98180\" srcset=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages.png 3568w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-150x66.png 150w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-560x247.png 560w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-80x35.png 80w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-768x338.png 768w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-1536x677.png 1536w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-2048x902.png 2048w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-1000x441.png 1000w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-650x286.png 650w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-300x132.png 300w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Types_Landing_Pages-160x70.png 160w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3568px) 100vw, 3568px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<div><p style=\"text-align:center; font-size:80%;\">The page on the left is a click-through landing page, while the one on the right is a lead gen landing page.</p></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Click-through landing pages prime visitors for the next step in their journey, like a checkout flow or sign-up page. Since the real ask comes wherever they end up <em>after </em>this page, the call to action here is simple—usually just a button. (&#8220;Buy Now&#8221; is a classic of this genre.) </p>\n\n\n\n<p>On the other hand, <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/lead-generation/high-converting-lead-generation-landing-page-examples/\">lead generation landing pages</a> use forms to capture visitor information that can be used later, like for promotional emails. These pages typically offer some kind of incentive (or “<a href=\"https://unbounce.com/lead-generation/lead-magnet-examples/\">lead magnet</a>”) for filling out the form—a downloadable ebook or webinar registration, for example.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>What about the design of a template?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>First, you need to decide whether your conversion goal requires a click-through or lead gen landing page. Then, <strong>consider</strong> <strong>how the template&#8217;s design spotlights your offer</strong>. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you’re selling soap, you probably want a click-through template that can accommodate lots of photos of your product, like <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-template/freshgoods/\">this one</a>. And maybe you think that soap-making webinar we suggested earlier sounds like a great idea. You might want a lead gen template that can share a video of what people can expect, like <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-template/multor/\">this one</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Notice that neither of these templates have anything to do with soap. We chose &#8217;em because <strong>their call to action supports our conversion goal and their design reinforces our offer</strong>. Now, we can start to replace elements of these pages with our own copy and imagery to integrate them into our marketing campaign.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Converting a Landing Page Template for Your Campaign</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Every landing page template is different, but they usually have similar elements and follow the same general structure: a header section, a list of features and benefits, some social proof, and a call to action.&#160;(Also check out this post on the <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-articles/the-anatomy-of-a-landing-page/\">anatomy of a landing page</a>.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Follow the steps below to <strong>transform your chosen template into a branded landing page that&#8217;ll win over your visitors</strong>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>1. Your Header Section</h3>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Add a hero image of your product, service, or lead magnet</strong>. If you want to help prospects visualize the benefits, consider showing your offer in the context of use: someone using your product to solve a problem or improving themselves through your service.&#160;</li><li><strong>Be sure to include your company logo</strong>. You want people to know this is your landing page, after all.&#160;</li><li><strong>Write a descriptive headline that tells people exactly what you’re offering</strong>. You can also communicate your main <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/conversion-glossary/definition/unique-value-proposition/\">value proposition</a> using a couple of sentences just under your headline.</li><li><strong>Update your call to action</strong>. If you’re using a click-through template, you could have a button that sends people to a product page on your website, a third-party delivery platform, or even add <a href=\"https://documentation.unbounce.com/hc/en-us/articles/203814024-Adding-a-Shopify-Buy-Button-to-Your-Landing-Page\">a Shopify integration</a>. If you’re capturing leads, try to keep your form simple—only ask for the information you absolutely need.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-98211\" srcset=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header.png 2880w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-150x67.png 150w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-557x250.png 557w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-80x36.png 80w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-768x345.png 768w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-1536x689.png 1536w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-2048x919.png 2048w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-1000x449.png 1000w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-650x292.png 650w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-300x135.png 300w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Promo_Header-160x72.png 160w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2880px) 100vw, 2880px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<div><p style=\"text-align:center; font-size:80%;\">This header from <a href=\"https://promo.com/\" target=\"_blank\"><font size=\"-1&#34;\">Promo</font></a> (featured in our post on <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-examples/high-converting-landing-pages/\"><font size=\"-1\">high-converting landing page examples</font></a>) communicates their offer super clearly.</p></div>\n\n\n\n<h3>2. Your Benefits Section </h3>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>People skim, so <strong>provide a bulleted list of the benefits of your offer</strong>. If you’re creating a sales page, use this space to highlight how your product or service improves your customers’ lives. If you’re offering a lead magnet (like an ebook), tell people what they’ll learn and how they can apply it.</li><li>Does your template have icons for each benefit? <strong>Make sure they’re relevant to your offer or brand</strong>. If not, lots of websites offer free icons you can use to replace ‘em: <a href=\"https://streamlineicons.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">streamlineicons.com</a>, <a href=\"https://www.flaticon.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">flaticon.com</a>, <a href=\"https://thenounproject.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">thenounproject.com</a>, <a href=\"https://material.io/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">material.io</a>, <a href=\"https://icons8.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">icons8.com</a>, <a href=\"https://ionicons.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">ionicons.com</a>, among others.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h3>3. Your Social Proof Section</h3>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Include a testimonial from a satisfied customer</strong>, or maybe an endorsement from an industry leader. The trick here is authenticity: use a real quote that <em>sounds</em> believable. Even real testimonials that are too positive can sound like you’re making ‘em up.&#160;</li><li>Alternatively, you could <strong>showcase other kinds of proof</strong>: awards you’ve won, trust seals you’ve earned—that sorta thing.</li><li>Whatever you include here, <strong>remember to ask permission</strong>. For example, depending on where you source a testimonial from (Amazon, G2), there may be restrictions on how you can use it.&#160;</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h3>4. Your About Section</h3>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Let people know more about your business</strong>. What makes your product or service unique? What’s your mission statement—your raison d&#8217;être? This is your opportunity to connect with visitors beyond this particular offer.</li><li>That said, you don&#8217;t want visitors to lose focus. <strong>Keep it short and sweet</strong>.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-98209\" srcset=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About.png 2880w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-150x80.png 150w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-470x250.png 470w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-80x43.png 80w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-768x409.png 768w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-1536x817.png 1536w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-2048x1089.png 2048w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-1000x532.png 1000w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-650x346.png 650w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-300x160.png 300w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/CocoVillage_About-160x85.png 160w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2880px) 100vw, 2880px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<div><p style=\"text-align:center; font-size:80%;\"><a href=\"https://cocovillage.ca/\" target=\"_blank\"><font size=\"-1&#34;\">Coco Village</font></a> (who we highlighted in our post on the <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-examples/best-landing-page-examples/\"><font size=\"-1\">best landing page examples</font></a>) blends social proof with their own parenting philosophy.</p></div>\n\n\n\n<h3>5. Your CTA Section</h3>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>If your page runs long, <strong>consider including a final pitch for your offer</strong>. This is your last chance, so make it count. Pump up the urgency or exclusivity, or remind visitors about the benefits they stand to gain—whatever it takes to get the conversion.</li><li><strong>Repeat the call to action button from your header section</strong>. Or, if this is a lead gen page, include a button that bumps visitors back up to your form.&#160;</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h3>6. Your Footer Section</h3>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Add your logo and any other details you need to communicate </strong>(contact information, copyright notice, any other necessary boilerplate) at the very bottom of the page.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>And that about covers it. With that quick checklist, you can turn just about any template into an on-brand landing page in just a few minutes. Simple, right?</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>3 (More) Examples of Landing Page Template Customization</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Alright, the soap example is feeling a little played out. Now, let’s take three templates that Unbounce put together in <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/news/working-for-you-during-covid-19/\">response to COVID-19</a> earlier this year—FreshGoods, Multor, and Horizons—and switch ‘em up for different industries.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can do all of this yourself, of course. But just to make sure these examples are <em>absolute fire</em>, I’ve recruited Gus from our design team to help out.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Gus says “what’s up,” by the way. <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f44b.png\" alt=\"👋\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /></p>\n\n\n\n<h2>FreshGoods → UNIQ</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-scaled.jpg\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-98148\" srcset=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-scaled.jpg 2117w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-124x150.jpg 124w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-207x250.jpg 207w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-66x80.jpg 66w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-768x929.jpg 768w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-1270x1536.jpg 1270w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-1694x2048.jpg 1694w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-1000x1209.jpg 1000w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-650x786.jpg 650w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-300x363.jpg 300w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Compare-132x160.jpg 132w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2117px) 100vw, 2117px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>First up is <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-template/freshgoods/\">FreshGoods</a>, a click-through landing page template that was designed to help brick-and-mortars get online super quick. Small retailers that don’t have a website can use it to launch a basic ecomm page. Restaurants and breweries can use it to link out to delivery platforms or run special promotions. But it can also fit a more general product launch page—say, for a new mobile app.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The design for FreshGoods clearly speaks to a bakery or cafe. You’ve got the hero image of a bread basket, secondary photography of hand-made pastries and specialty coffees, plus icons that imply food delivery.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/FreshGoods_Full.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Thumb_FreshGoods.jpg\" alt=\"Landing Page Template Examples - FreshGoods\" class=\"wp-image-98146\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">The original version of <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-template/freshgoods/\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">FreshGoods</a>. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>But what’s great about FreshGoods is that it’s both<strong> simple and comprehensive</strong>. You’ve got all the sections you need to communicate your offer in a compelling way, without any of the technical design elements you’d need to spend hours tinkering with.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Changing it up is <em>super easy</em>. You’ve really just gotta swap in your logo, images, and icons—then you’ve got (what looks like) a totally custom landing page.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_FreshGoods_Revised-scaled.jpg\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Thumb_App.jpg\" alt=\"Landing Page Template Examples - FreshGoods (Revised)\" class=\"wp-image-98145\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">The new landing page we built with FreshGoods. (Click to see the whole thing.)</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Sure, when you compare the two pages side-by-side, you can see they’re similar. But think about the amount of real work that went into this. Swapping in the new logo? Two minutes. Sourcing images… say 10 minutes. (Or even less, considering our in-app <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/product/integrations/unsplash/\">integration with Unsplash</a>.) Add a couple other minor tweaks, and what you’re looking at is, like, 20 minutes for a whole new page.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>All you’ve gotta do now is write your campaign copy. (And if you want tips on how to write for your industry, you can pull some insights from our <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/conversion-benchmark-report/\">Conversion Benchmark Report</a>.)</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Multor → PersonalTrainer</h2>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-scaled.jpg\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-98147\" srcset=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-scaled.jpg 2117w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-124x150.jpg 124w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-207x250.jpg 207w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-66x80.jpg 66w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-768x929.jpg 768w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-1270x1536.jpg 1270w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-1694x2048.jpg 1694w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-1000x1209.jpg 1000w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-650x786.jpg 650w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-300x363.jpg 300w, https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Compare-132x160.jpg 132w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2117px) 100vw, 2117px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>The idea for the <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-template/multor/\">Multor</a> lead gen template was to help businesses offer digital alternatives to their in-person services. Healthcare clinics and dentists can use it to offer online consultations. Realtors can schedule people for virtual home walkthroughs. Fitness instructors can register people for video classes… which gives us a great idea for a new page.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>We’ll get to that in a second, but let’s have a look at the original page first. Multor Senior feels pretty Silicon Valley, right? It’s all photos of people on computers. (We even snuck a coffee in there, which is <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.shutterstock.com/search/coffee%2Btech?section=1&#38;image_type=photo&#38;ref_context=keyword\" target=\"_blank\">very tech</a>.) And the blue is evoking logic and dependability. Look, there it goes!</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Multor_Full.png\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Thumb_Multor.jpg\" alt=\"Landing Page Template Examples - Multor\" class=\"wp-image-98150\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">The original version of <a href=\"https://unbounce.com/landing-page-template/multor/\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Multor</a>. To create our new fitness landing page, we just added our logo and hero image, changed the icons, and replaced the old photos and video. Then we tinkered with some of the fonts, colors, and backgrounds.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full is-resized\"><a class=\"fancybox iframelpexamples\" href=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Full_Multor_Revised-scaled.jpg\" target=\"_blank\"><img src=\"https://mk0zofoqaluvgdskgvsb.kinstacdn.com/photos/Thumb_PersonalTrainer.jpg\" alt=\"Landing Page Template Examples - Multor (Revised)\" class=\"wp-image-98154\" width=\"1182\" height=\"597\"></a><figcaption class=\"blog-photo-annotation\">The new landing page we built with Multor.
